<span id="freeTextContainer5446517786998869481">This was read for /r/fantasy's book bingo, at the insistent shilling of Para.<br/><br/>I'm a mixed bag on this review. The book was brilliant in many ways--but the payoff/effort ratio hurt it, a lot. I would probably feel comfortable giving it five stars, easily, on my next readthrough, but it's a CHONK and I don't have the luxury of a re-read now. <br/><br/>My other issue with the book was, unfortunately, its characters. Some of them grated on me that made reading their sections more of a chore than a pleasure. An</span>
  <span id="freeText5446517786998869481" style="display:none">This was read for /r/fantasy's book bingo, at the insistent shilling of Para.<br /><br />I'm a mixed bag on this review. The book was brilliant in many ways--but the payoff/effort ratio hurt it, a lot. I would probably feel comfortable giving it five stars, easily, on my next readthrough, but it's a CHONK and I don't have the luxury of a re-read now. <br /><br />My other issue with the book was, unfortunately, its characters. Some of them grated on me that made reading their sections more of a chore than a pleasure. And for books like this, they live and die on their characters.<br /><br />Some of the sections feel like fever dreams (because in a way, they are) and even upon finishing it, I have many questions. Many of these are "good," but some of them just baffled me. I'm not sure how much of that was lost in translation, because the book was very well translated. <br /><br />If you don't mind wallowing through 500+ dense pages to get to the goods, this book might be for you. If you wanted <i>Vita Nostra</i> with a much larger scope and an ending, this book might be for you. Because, at the end, when all the pieces come together, you feel both like an idiot (sometimes) and a genius (most of the time) for putting them together.<br /><br />If you want to read this for bingo (bless you, with 20 days left), you'll find this square fills: disability, slice-of-life, twins, rec (Para will shill relentlessly), and local author to Yerevan (Armenia).</span>

<div id="review_2969761699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2969761699" />
    <a title="Beatrix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12397138-beatrix"><img alt="Beatrix" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378654912p2/12397138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2969761699?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrix" href="/user/show/12397138-beatrix">Beatrix</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789631430004" href="/book/show/23365753-abban-a-h-zban">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2969761699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9711554961359138258">I guess you must be in the right frame of mind to accept this book, or the book to accept you (but let's not get mystical).<br/>When I first started reading it, about three years ago, I never got further than the end of the first part, and reading the first part took me about two months. I remember thinking at that time that it's amazing - all the words are perfect and beautiful and unexpected yet right where they need to be. But still - I didn't go on. (Or couldn't.)<br/><br/>This time, I knew from the start </span>
  <span id="freeText9711554961359138258" style="display:none">I guess you must be in the right frame of mind to accept this book, or the book to accept you (but let's not get mystical).<br />When I first started reading it, about three years ago, I never got further than the end of the first part, and reading the first part took me about two months. I remember thinking at that time that it's amazing - all the words are perfect and beautiful and unexpected yet right where they need to be. But still - I didn't go on. (Or couldn't.)<br /><br />This time, I knew from the start that it's going to be different - and it was.<br />And I was mesmerized.<br />By.<br /><br />The sunniness of the House.<br />The darkness of it.<br />The unknown, that wants to be known.<br />The reincarnations &amp; reinventions &amp; the reimaginings of lives.<br />The eternal inventiveness and playfulness.<br />The legends and myths and landmarks and crossovers and crossroads and the power of words - because if someone with the eyes to see gives you a name, you will become that name.<br />The confinement - where the whole world is just a few rooms and a corridor and a courtyard - but oh damn, the whole world <i>can</i> fit there. It's in your head anyway - isn't it?<br /><br />Still.<br /><br />Even though I knew that this time, I was going to finish it, it still wasn't easy. This is a magical monster book - like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24800.House_of_Leaves" title="House of Leaves by Mark Z. Danielewski" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Leaves</a> (accidentally, that's also about a house) - a very uncomfortable book which occupies both my waking and sleeping mind, and it's not a book to <i>do</i> casually, it's a book where you need to be pushed, sometimes even brutally, to climb better, understand better, look closer, listen closer, because look and listen you must.<br /><br />With this I'm not saying that reading this novel is not a pleasure. It is a pleasure, a most exquisite kind. Not the easy and straightforward kind.<br /><br />After reading it (it only took me about a month now, for the whole book), I immediately wanted to go back and start it again. I need my memory to go backward and forward at the same time to understand everything here. And because I want to understand, I'll return. And again, just like it happened with the House of Leaves, I suspect this is gonna become another home for me, a place I'll keep returning to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9711554961359138258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2203560766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203560766" />
    <a title="Stephanie Jane (Literary Flits)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31264299-stephanie-jane-literary-flits"><img alt="Stephanie Jane (Literary Flits)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497004324p2/31264299.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2203560766?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Jane (Literary Flits)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Jane (Literary Flits)" href="/user/show/31264299-stephanie-jane-literary-flits">Stephanie Jane (Literary Flits)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31264299-stephanie-jane-literary-flits?shelf=fiction-asia">fiction-asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203560766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3175659620554405540">See more of my book reviews on my blog, <a href='http://litflits.blogspot.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Literary Flits</a><br/><br/>I received my review copy of The Gray House back at the beginning of 2017 but, being intimidated by its 700+ page length, kept putting off even starting to read it until now. This was a serious mistake - The Gray House is absolutely brilliant! Seclude-yourself-for-a-week-with-your-phone-turned-off breathtakingly brilliant! I could easily write a whole review of fangirl superlatives, I loved this book that much. Yet, that said, it won't be to </span>
  <span id="freeText3175659620554405540" style="display:none">See more of my book reviews on my blog, <a href="http://litflits.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary Flits</a><br /><br />I received my review copy of The Gray House back at the beginning of 2017 but, being intimidated by its 700+ page length, kept putting off even starting to read it until now. This was a serious mistake - The Gray House is absolutely brilliant! Seclude-yourself-for-a-week-with-your-phone-turned-off breathtakingly brilliant! I could easily write a whole review of fangirl superlatives, I loved this book that much. Yet, that said, it won't be to everyone's taste. I have seen other reviews using The Lord Of The Flies as a comparison and inasmuch as that book centres on a group of unaccompanied boys I can see their point, but I wouldn't necessarily agree. Perhaps if Salman Rushdie had written Gormenghast the result might be closer to the fantastic and fantastical richness of The Gray House?<br /><br />I obviously want to impart as much of my enthusiasm as possible, but am struggling to describe Petrosyan's novel in a way that will do it justice! It is set in a neglected House for physically disabled children, children who have mostly been effectively abandoned there by their families so, other than attempts at lessons, the tribes of boys (and, later, girls) are left to their own devices. Living by complex sets of rules and Laws, we see their limited world through their own eyes. I loved that this world is limited by the borders of the House, not by the various disabilities. Ingenuity, inventiveness and camaraderie seem to render most disability irrelevant.<br /><br />The story is told from different points of view, some first person and some third person, with each speaker having their own distinctive voices. The Gray House is divided into three books each with their own lengthy character list at the beginning, but I didn't bother with the lists as I soon found myself easily identifying and remembering characters by their Nicks (nicknames) and actions. Like new boy Grasshopper, it took me a while to settle into the House, but once I began to understand its ways and its stories, I was absolutely engrossed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3175659620554405540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16440263038611717207" style="display:none">(original review copied at the bottom)<br /><br />Adding on for this (Audible) review --<br /><br />I plan to read Kipling's "The Jungle Book" (because of Tabaqui and other references), and Carroll's "The Hunting of the Snark" (because of multiple chapter epigraphs), first, before reading the physical book.<br /><br />Having a hard time making clear which editions were read when. <div id="review_2023137405" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023137405" />
    <a title="Sherry Elmer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20805054-sherry-elmer"><img alt="Sherry Elmer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369803487p2/20805054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023137405?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherry Elmer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherry Elmer" href="/user/show/20805054-sherry-elmer">Sherry Elmer</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20805054-sherry-elmer?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20805054-sherry-elmer?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20805054-sherry-elmer?shelf=russian">russian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023137405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8782100992838256640">This book seems like two different books rolled into one to me. One is a beautiful story of a group of children, all with some disability, who grow up in an old, gray house where they learn to create their own rules, fend for themselves, and care for one another. I found this book to be very good, with unique, imaginative, fully-drawn characters. I could imagine myself hanging out with many of the characters and truly enjoying myself.<br/><br/>The “other” book is a supernatural story of a house which infl</span>
  <span id="freeText8782100992838256640" style="display:none">This book seems like two different books rolled into one to me. One is a beautiful story of a group of children, all with some disability, who grow up in an old, gray house where they learn to create their own rules, fend for themselves, and care for one another. I found this book to be very good, with unique, imaginative, fully-drawn characters. I could imagine myself hanging out with many of the characters and truly enjoying myself.<br /><br />The “other” book is a supernatural story of a house which influences its inhabitants as much as it is influenced by them. There are odd happenings and irregularities in time, place, and essence. For me, this book did not work. I did not find the ending satisfactory, and in fact felt cheated. For so many chapters I worried along with the characters about the coming graduation, fearful, like them, that something dreadful was going to happen. And then... nothing. I don't require books to tie up loose ends, and I certainly don't require a happy ending, but I do want an ending. This book felt more abandoned than completed. And I may be the only one who feels this way, but I felt the book would have been stronger and better had it not included the supernatural aspects. The students of the gray house are people I am thankful to have met, but I could have done without some of the plot elements. <br /><br /><br /><br /> THE STRANGER			<br />ALBERT CAMUS<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8782100992838256640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+xmopz5tgR3oS77eCfhhIYl/jDydKckNRaYBzhDEGvnBP8F1hTNIdU9gCr/+DWv+XyBr9FOkR2oe2Ed/3YfoYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fAGwtSXjDEjO/mDzQ3/wVmfY0lbgcYyUd43AK0miJa5GJ9lnnr3FIGnV1JK0ivqJsYc1ni78AvMs84aahOHXNA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6771166325513287997">Following college, Mariam Petrosyan became a cartoonist at the Studio of Armenfilm in 1989. She subsequently moved to Moscow and worked at Soyuzmultfilm Studio. In 1995, she returned to Armenfilm, where she worked until 2007. She is married to Artashes Stamboltsan. They have two children. She is a great-granddaughter of the Armenian painter Martiros Saryan.</span>
